class='widget Header' id='Header1'> <div id='header-inner'> <div class='titlewrapper'> <h1 class='title'> <a href='http://althouse.blogspot.com/'>Althouse</a> </h1> </div> <div class='descriptionwrapper'> <p class='description'><span><a href="http://althouse.blogspot.com/p/about-ann-althouse.html">Who is Althouse?</a> * <a href="http://althouse.blogspot.com/search/label/law">View only LAW posts</a> * <a href="http://althouse.blogspot.com/p/support-althouse-through-amazon.html">Contribute</a> * <a class='blog-posts hfeed'> <!-- google_ad_section_start(name=default) -->            <div class="date-outer">          <h2 class='date-header'><span>August 6, 2015</span></h2>            <div class="date-posts">          <div class='post-outer'> <div class='post hentry'> <a name='5600969419294750137'></a> <h3 class='post-title entry-title'> <a href='http://althouse.blogspot.com/2015/08/i-was-sure-this-was-anti-abortion.html'>I was sure this was an anti-abortion illustration &#8212; a pretty peevish, nasty one &#8212;&#160;and I'm still finding it hard to believe the NYT used it for a pro-choice op-ed.</a> </h3> <div class='post-header-line-1'></div> <div class='post-body entry-content'> <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-q9FI1mpCYgM/VcNZjpbUfTI/AAAAAAAAD-4/4u4Wu-wY2c4/s1600/meg.tiff" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="200" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-q9FI1mpCYgM/VcNZjpbUfTI/AAAAAAAAD-4/4u4Wu-wY2c4/s200/meg.tiff" width="181" /></a><br /> <br /> That's a snippet of the illustration &#8212; by Ruth Gwily &#8212; which you can see enlarged and in full <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2015/08/05/opinion/how-to-really-defend-planned-parenthood.html">here</a>. The op-ed, by Katha Pollitt, is <a href="http://nyti.ms/1KPLLr1">"How to Really Defend Planned Parenthood."</a> Pollitt's op-ed is somewhat interesting, because she does seem to be struggling over what to think and how to talk about abortion in the wake of the disturbing Planned Parenthood videos. ("[T]he videos do cleverly evoke visceral feelings of disgust &#8212; graphic images, physicians using the words 'crush' and 'crunchy' &#8212; to activate the stereotype that abortion providers are money-grubbing baby killers.") Pollitt wants pro-choice people to speak up, loud and clear, rather than to keep their head down and only pipe up when there's something &#8212; like these videos &#8212; that needs a response. But in the end, I don't think Pollitt has said anything that will change the low-profile of the pro-choice crowd.<br /> <blockquote class="tr_bq"> We need to say that women have sex, have abortions, are at peace with the decision and move on with their lives. We need to say that is their right, and, moreover, it&#8217;s good for everyone that they have this right: The whole society benefits when motherhood is voluntary. When we gloss over these truths we unintentionally promote the very stigma we&#8217;re trying to combat... </blockquote> There are truths on both sides, pro-life and pro-choice, and the truths on the pro-life side lend themselves to loud, passionate assertion. On the pro-choice side, there's more reason to exercise restraint. These are hard truths. <i>The whole society benefits when motherhood is voluntary</i> can be paraphrased as <i>That dead baby would have been a bad citizen anyway</i>. And the pro-choice side got its passion extracted when abortion became a right. Rights are supposed to make you feel secure, and, feeling secure, why should you have to yell about what you want anymore?<br /> <br /> But let's talk about that illustration. I thought some right-wing website was portraying feminists as creepy, ugly jerks! The rat teeth, the sneering nose, the greasy, stringy hair, the misshapen ear that seems twisted a few notches to the left. That's the pro-choice image of a pro-choice woman?! I don't get it. Why make her repulsive?<br /> <br /> It also makes no sense to use a tiny megaphone to express the idea that her voice is not being heard. Pro-choicers can get all the social and mainstream amplification they want. They are <i>choosing</i> to be low-key. That's Pollitt's point!<br /> <br /> I'm assuming that you immediately perceive the thing in the woman's hand as a megaphone. I called Meade over to look at the illustration, and at first glance, he "saw" a little baby about to be eaten by the woman.<br /> <br /> I did a Google image search for a megaphone to get an idea of how accurate the illustration is and I came up with <a href="http://advocatesaz.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/02/pr-megaphone.jpg">this Planned Parenthood image</a>:<br /> <br /> <a href="http://advocatesaz.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/02/pr-megaphone.jpg" imageanchor="1"><img border="0" src="http://advocatesaz.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/02/pr-megaphone.jpg" height="276" width="320" /></a><br /> <br /> I strongly suspect that Ruth Gwily (the illustrator) used that photo as her reference. I think it explains the protruding teeth and the sneering nose. It seemed, I'm guessing, like a good idea to turn the pretty model into a "real" woman, and nobody with decision-making authority had the perspective to notice how awful she looked. <div style='clear: both;'></div> </div> <div class='post-footer'> <div class='post-footer-line post-footer-line-1'><span class='post-author vcard'> Posted by <span class='fn'>Ann Althouse</span> </span> <span If they&#39;re setting up a nursery and buying little baseball mitts, the fetus has a soul.  It&#39;s part of a life.<br /><br />If not, not.<br /><br />When a baby is born, it has relations to all of society who are wired to want to care for it.  That&#39;s a relation too.  That&#39;s why birth is a bright line.  It lines up with society&#39;s interests.<br /><br />To the extent that a fetus can be pictured as baby-like, you can push this line back into the pregnancy.<br /><br />It some point that becomes dishonest.  Those wanting to care for the baby don&#39;t want to care for the baby, but only want one thing : that the fetus not be aborted.  A theoretical fact rather than a comittment.  It goes dogmatic.<br /><br />So some line will be drawn, the baby picturers against the mineral rights claimed against the mother.<br /><br />The discovery of a dishonest argument pushing the line one way or the other is not to be celebrated, though. </p> </dd> <dd class='comment-footer'> <span class='comment-timestamp'> <a href='http://althouse.blogspot.com/2015/08/i-was-sure-this-was-anti-abortion.html?showComment=1438876603761#c2683840529245520534' title='comment permalink'> 8/6/15, 10:56 AM </a> <span class='item-control blog-admin pid-1776835017'> <a class='comment-delete' href='https://www.blogger.com/delete-comment.g?blogID=6329595&postID=2683840529245520534' title='Delete Comment'> <img src='//www.blogger.com/img/icon_delete13.gif'/> </a> </span> </span> </dd> <dt class='comment-author ' id='c5794244434123787668'> <a name='c5794244434123787668'></a> <div class="avatar-image-container vcard"><span dir="ltr"><a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/00936808380090258703" rel="nofollow" onclick="" class="avatar-hovercard" id="av-73-00936808380090258703"><img src="https://img1.blogblog.com/img/blank.gif" width="35" height="35" alt="" class="delayLoad" style="display: none;" longdesc="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_NjrNTiyYuV0/ShbR4FKVmuI/AAAAAAAAABw/Y-Svufyp3JY/S45-s35/MJB_SMPier.jpg" title="Mike">  <noscript><img src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_NjrNTiyYuV0/ShbR4FKVmuI/AAAAAAAAABw/Y-Svufyp3JY/S45-s35/MJB_SMPier.jpg" width="35" height="35" class="photo" alt=""></noscript></a></span></div> <a href='https://www.blogger.com/profile/00936808380090258703' rel='nofollow'>Mike</a> said... </dt> <dd class='comment-body' id='Blog1_cmt-5794244434123787668'> <p> About dishonest arguments, they are much easier to direct when there are few facts to base assertions upon. PPA has worked hard to get women to believe that abortion merely removes undefined &quot;products of conception.&quot; What many of us who are more honest knew, and these videos show quite graphically, is that abortion kills a baby, whose human organs are then harvested (at some profit) for medical research. The legalities aside, we see clearly (some of us, anyway) that abortion is a dreadfully immoral and grotesque practice that is aggressively, even angrily, defended aggressively women who are willing to go as far as necessary to enjoy their sexuality while remaining unencumbered by motherhood. The graphic is ugly, but what is being defended is downright hideous.   </p> </dd> <dd class='comment-footer'> <span class='comment-timestamp'> <a Most plainly the PP people on tape discuss the widely varying cost/price for different parts/organs.  Since the shipping costs for these parts are VERY unlikely to differ much (a fetal heart should cost about the same to ship as a fetal liver, etc) and since the PP people don&#39;t put the cost differential down to any difference in the cost of extracting or obtaining the parts/organs, it&#39;s very obvious that something other than &quot;shipping and handling&quot; is driving the price PP receives for the parts.  That something, of course, is the market price for the organ (determined by the intersection of supply and demand, don&#39;cha&#39;know), which means &quot;dealing&quot; in those parts (selling them, arranging for their sale, agreeing to a price, etc) should properly be considered engaging in commerce.<br />I acknowledge the argument, but it&#39;s false on its face.
